RATING: 7
It plays very different depending on the number of players, with 4-5 it takes a good bluffing for the saboteurs to win, with 6-10 is can be a little chaotic and all depends more on luck that other thing. I prefer a small group, but both options are fun, besides is small, fast and easy to teach.

RATING: 7.5
Juego ideal para días de campo o fiestas familiares, hasta 10 jugadores, simple y rapido de pillar, ameno, adictivo. Tres rondas de este juego pueden llegar a la media hora si se esta jugando con 8 jugadores o más, si son menos, puedes terminar en torno a 10 minutos antes. 
El juego tiene mucho juego en grupos,empiezas la partida dudando de todos, y conforme se va adentrando en la cueva, se empieza a dividir el grupo en dos, aunque siempre hay alguien que te hace dudar. Muy bueno para el precio que tiene, unos 10 euros. Por cierto que hay web chinas que lo ofrecen a unos 5 o 6 euros envio incluido, las cartas no tienen dependencia de idioma, y las instrucciones se encuentran en cualquier sitio.
Si te juntas con familia o amigos en grupos y quereis echar una media hora simpatica es perfecto.

RATING: 8.5
This is a really fun game.  Maybe it's one of those that anyone who regularly plays games with 6 or more people should own.  You can play it with less players but it's best with 6 .  There are a lot of subtle strategies in this - mostly concerning the timing of when and where you play certain cards and sometimes about sending others subtle hints about what you're doing or what you know - for instance, if you're a digging-dwarf, blocking or making it tougher to use the path to a finish card you know to be a rock. But there again, players have to read whether someone else's first movements are a subterfuge or for real.  You can be sure that experienced saboteurs will not reveal themselves quickly or easily!  

A lot of fun for a little money.

RATING: 7
A coop card game with a betrayal mechanic that doesn't take too long to play and has a light theme about mining. The game plays like a conflict based waterworks where you are all trying to build tunnels to three possible pay days with one real one. Saboteurs get involved, equipment gets sabotaged, things get real.

RATING: 6
It's really nice to have a game which handles up to 10 players, but our plays so far have not been that great. The Saboteurs always EASILY won the game (the opposite result that most people report here), but I can't find anything we were doing wrong!  Hopefully, more play will reveal the play balance and be more fun.
Update 2005 05 14: The chances for the saboteurs change pretty dramatically bases on the number of players. Our original plays were using the worst odds, whereas my latest plays have been the opposite. I like it well enough, but it's too bad it's not better balanced.

RATING: 8
Different roles, different objectives. Roles are dealt randomly to player. A dwarf will have to build a continuous, uninterupted path to the gold mine. Saboteurs will have to prevent the dwarves to do so. The game consists of path cards, both normal and dead end. There are red special cards to stop players from playing path cards and green ones to 'free' player so that they can continue playing path cards. Map cards to take a peek on the 3 possible face down card as only 1 is the gold mine. And finally, the explosive card, to destroy the path card.
 
Fun, fun, fun game. Because nobody knows who are the dwarves or the saboteurs, making the table conversation very interesting. Players will try to give hints and sign languages to show their allegiance. Lots of lying and lots of poker faces for sure. So be prepared to be cracking your head, figuring out who's who.

And the game can be player from 3-10 players making it a good game for big groups.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.8
A game that is easy to play and learn.  A semi-cooperative game divided into 2.  One party consists of good dwarves trying to dig for gold when the other party of saboteurs is trying to prevent them from reaching the gold.

Besides building cards which builds the tunnel to reach the goal, there are map cards which players can peek at 1 of the 3 goal cards to see if they are gold or stones.  Earthquake cards that allows players to destroy 1 building cards played.  Freeze cards and unfreeze cards are there to prevent and allow players to build the tunnel respectively.

Good points: Easy to learn and fun to play.

Bad points: The fun of the game mostly resides in the saboteur side.  Almost all the players wishes to be the saboteurs.  Uneven winning chances as there is a higher percentage that the saboteurs will win.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.3
Although very simple, this game is fun. I think the game is well balanced. With 1 saboteur the game is harder for this player, but if he wins he wins big (4 gold nuggets). If 2 or 3 saboteurs are present it is easier for them, but they only win 3 gold nuggets each. And with 4 saboteurs they only win 2 gold nuggets each.
From 3 to 10 players.

There are some strategies for the saboteur player(s). 

1st - If you can look at, early in the game, a goal card (at this point you know where the gold is, it's either on the card you've seen or in one of the other two) you can direct efforts towards a (false) card and thus making the good players lose precious time, this is the most efective way to win, I think, because you play as though you're trying to win.

2nd - you can buy time, not adding a path card and building up your block cards, if you can block other players you can stop their progress, of course that other players will block you immediately, but since being blocked only prevents you from playing path cards, you can still continue to block other players.

3rd - you can destroy a path card that is in such a position that is very dificult to find a replacement and thus making the other players lose precious time trying to fill that empty space with an apropriate card, even better if you happen to have another of those boulder cards, after players find a matching card for that place, you immediately destroy it again, at that time it will be almost impossible for the good guys to win.

usually a good saboteur player will try to do a mixture of the 3 options, meaning: trying to mislead the other players into a worthless goal card, accumulating block cards, and holding on to the special cards that destroy path cards and playing them at the right time.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Less obvious who is who than Bang!, easier to learn, faster to play, and everyone stays at the table. Variants (no gold for dwarves with broken equipment, saboteurs know each other, treasures at different distances, etc.) increase the options, and flexibility is always nice. The scoring system (where an individual player wins the overall game even though each round is played in teams) makes sense to me (it rewards the best player over multiple rounds), but has proved confusing to a couple crowds; in those situations, most people didn't really care who was the overall winner after a few rounds and didn't even bother counting their gold. Perhaps this is a testament to how fun the game is: players didn't even care who won (even though they took gold after each round), but were just happy to play the game. At any rate, Saboteur is a [i]lot[/i] of fun with the right crowd, but you do have to assess whether you have the right group of people before breaking this out or it won't meet its potential. This is a wickedly fun game in a small package – very underrated on BGG, and very worth checking out. 

Variants used: (i) good dwarves with broken equipment do not receive gold; (ii) saboteurs know who each other are; (iii) center goal card is one space further from the ladder; (iv) first player to [i]x[/i] points wins ([i]x[/i]=10, or some other number depending on desired game length). (2008-10)

RATING: 7
This is the only hidden role game I've ever played but I do enjoy it a lot and love to see the maze form.

To combat the frustration of having a broken tool and nothing to fix it with for a whole round, I recommend borrowing a rule from Saboteur 2 that allows you to fix the tool by discarding a card from your hand. You then play the remainder of the round with 1 fewer cards in hand. Of course, if you opt for this, you will draw the card to fix the tool almost immediately afterward, in keeping with Murphy's Law of Card Games (I made that up--don't bother googling it).

It's great fun, fast and well balanced.  I'm quite impressed with this one.

RATING: 6
The tug of war that you feel in this game is quite nice, but it's often easy to pick out who are the saboteurs based on their actions.  It also doesn't evenly reward the successful miners which seems unfair.  I'm not sure if we will play this game on a regular basis, but for a once-in-a-while game it's a real blast.  Unfortunately, Rikki hates it and has declared that she will never play again, which doesn't bode well for the future of the game.

There seems to be a distinct difference in the feel of this game depending on the number of players.  With more players the saboteurs can remain hidden better.  However, if fate makes it so that there are not many saboteurs, they will struggle to slow down the miners.  I think my favorite part of the game is that players can help other players, and even flat-out lie.  With a good group of liars the fun is definitely amped up in this game.

RATING: 5
I was disappointed by Saboteur, for this isn’t the game I was told it was: it’s quick, easy and light-hearted, I agree; yet it’s just remotely fun and, most of all, its gameplay is pretty bugged: actually the traitor element has been developed only superficially, for after just a couple of turns it’s pretty obvious who the saboteurs are. And from that point on the game becomes a rush to prevent them from playing, often successfully.

The whole game feels like an «uncollaborative cooperative»: Saboteur looks like a cooperative game indeed but doesn’t make for a cooperative play because of the way dwarves receive and share the gold cards when reaching the goldmine. Okay, dwarven greed is notorious, yet Saboteur’s dwarves look more like David the Gnome than D&D’s, so this victory points mechanics feels just out of place.

A longer review can be read [url=http://boardgamegeek.com/article/7869714]here[/url].

RATING: 4
I think people are starting to come around that this just isn't a very good game. It's not subtle enough: either you know exactly what someone is or you have no clue. It's also too much of a bad play to damage someone as your only option on your turn. Think about an 8-player game: you spend your one turn (of say 5 or 6 you'll get) to damage one other player, leaving 6 other players to perform actions that help them better than what you just did helped you.

The scoring is pretty wonky too with the blue vs green dwarves. I think the original game might actually be better, but I've really soured on this in general of late.

Don't remember all the scores, but I won with 4 gold due to having the sole Geologist in the first round and lots of gems came out - even though I never played one and had almost nothing to do with the game's outcome. I'd rather play Slide 5 any day; at least there's more you can do to actually affect your position!!

RATING: 8
A great, chaotic filler game for a crowd. We enjoyed the game a lot but had a few gripes with it. If one of you're tools are damaged and you don't have the card to fix it, you cannot do anything but beg for other players' mercy. And the gold distribution is very random.

We house-ruled the gold distribution such that the one who finishes the tunnel to the gold gets 3 gold, all other dwarfs get 2, unless they have broken tools then they only get 1. If the saboteurs win they always get 2. 

Both issues are fixed by the Saboteur 2 expansion, which also comes with new roles and new cards and overall makes this great game even much better.

RATING: 6
Updated 10/30/10.

[thing=9220]Saboteur[/thing] is a mediocre hidden-role, teamwork/traitor card game in which players assume the role of miners extending a network of tunnels in the search for a hidden vein of gold.  It is also a very good example of wasted design potential.  

Saboteur is played over three rounds.  Before each round, one or two miners are secretly assigned the role of Saboteur, and will only win if the remaining miners are unable to connect the mine to the vein of gold.  If the Saboteurs are successful, they get a windfall.  If the miners are successful in discovering the gold, they all share in the reward, with the miner having played the winning card getting a relatively larger cut. 

I like the idea of a reasonably short (45-minute), tense, role-deduction game, and Saboteur's central premise and core mechanisms seem well-adapted to that end.  However, Saboteur is ultimately damned by imbalanced incentives and needless randomness. 

The entire idea of a hidden-role/traitor game (or at least the only part of the idea that I consider to be worth building a game around) is that the traitor should be able to impede the success of the team while appearing to be working for them, leading to mistrust, accusations, and in-fighting.  Here, the deck gives the Saboteur player three tools to prevent building.  But two of them -- rockfalls and dead-ends -- would never be played by a conscientious miner.  Consequently, playing one of these cards is a clear give-away that you're the Saboteur. (And if you're outed early, you're extremely unlikely to win.)  To some extent, this flaw turns on the fact that the game allows players to discard a card in lieu of their turn, meaning miners are never forced to play a sub-optimal card.    

Broken tool cards are a different story, at least.  The third weapon in the Saboteur's bag of tricks, a broken tool prevents the miner it is played against from building any further tunnels until the tool is fixed.  An optional rule (I have no idea why this is optional) prevents miners with broken tool cards from sharing in the treasure if the team succeeds.  Thus, unlike rockfalls and dead-ends, the miner players, at least have some incentives to employ broken tool cards against each other, when nearing the end of a round.  The problem with broken tools, however, is that they are disastrously random (a broken tool comes in one of three types and may only be fixed by a repair card of matching type).  The effect of playing a broken tool turns almost entirely on whether that particular player happened to get one of the few repair cards with a matching symbol, which is nothing more than dumb luck.    

As a card game, I was excited by the potential need for clever hand management, but there is no need.  Most of the tunnel cards are relatively effective at extending the tunnel most of the time, so players are strongly incentivized to simply hoard repair cards and broken tools, playing whatever tunnel they happen to draw.  The whole thing is a imbalanced mess that lacks much interest or tension beyond the first few hands.  In the games I've played, the Sabateurs never win, either because the hidden information doesn't remain hidden long enough, or because keeping it hidden brings the miners too close to victory too soon. 

While I certainly still prefer Saboteur to much of the cartoony dross that passes for filler these days (e.g. [thing=116]Guillotine[/thing], [thing=1927]Munchkin[/thing], [thing=770]Loot[/thing]), it disappoints in large part because it obviously could have been so much better.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4
This is not a hidden traitor game. Hidden traitor implies, well, hidden. But the saboteurs lack the tools to hide. All of their tools are out there in the open. We see everything they do.

And there isn't much they can do. They are badly outnumbered, and it's really just a question of cards. The saboteurs have to get really lucky with their card draws in order to either draw a majority of the forward progress cards so that the goal cards can't be reached (or a combination of them plus rock slides).

So the game only has bite if the dwarves fight over who gets to draw gold first. But unless it's the last round, I think most dwarves in the first and second round are just hoping that the other dwarf players draw saboteur cards in the final round. Because all too often the dwarves are content to get the gold, even if it means getting last pick.

RATING: 4
Picked this up after hearing it called "the new Bang!" Pretty disappointing. It's boring, and the gold collection at the end feels tacked on and clunky. The need to play several rounds to determine a winner doesn't work for what should be a light little game. The hidden role mechanic is at its worst here... it's extremely difficult to hide that you're the Saboteur for long, mainly because the game doesn't give the dwarves enough incentive to repeatedly harm their rivals (especially not when they could be furthering themselves). In the rare circumstances that we have 9 or 10 people around for games this could work, but beyond that I'll stick with Bang!

RATING: 8
Much prefer this to Bang (which also has secret identities) - much shorter and no elimination. Only 5 minutes to explain, 40 minutes for the three rounds and handles up to 10 players! This game needs to be played with accusations flying and plenty of speculation about who the saboteurs are, so works much better with friends. Played in a polite silence, this would be awfully dull.

Variants: Non-saboteur dwarfs who have been sabotaged (by anyone) do not share in the gold if the dwarfs win. (This encourages dwarfs to become a bit greedy and sabotage their own side when they come close to winning) and can add a bit of uncertainty as to who the saboteurs really are. Also put one or even two map cards aside. If everyone knows where the gold is the game is a lot less exciting.

RATING: 7
A game of sabotage packaged in three short courses.  Much of this game is luck:  the cards you draw (miner: "I had a great saboteur hand the entire time!!"), the number of saboteurs (too few saboteurs usually leads to a runaway victory for the good guys), the arrangement of players around the table (for when the good guys pass the loot around).  It's still fun and (sometimes) quick, and since roles are recycled each round, most players get a shot at playing both sides during the course of the game.  Most of the games I've played have been with a large number of players (6+), and I feel that the deck runs out too quickly in these cases.

RATING: 6
Although the premise of the game is nice enough, its execution fails because not only does luck play a huge part in this game (e.g. saboteurs not getting any dead ends or special cards), it also depends on the saboteur(s) being able to stay hidden. When all non-saboteurs just go full co-op, this is simply impossible. One lone saboteur will have a very hard time winning at any rate.

The rule swapping after each round is not very effective.

In my opinion, some cards should have a different effect for a saboteur player than for miner players. This way, despite their identity being revealed even faster, lone saboteurs would at least stand a fighting chance. A good example would be a saboteur being able to discard three random cards to obtain the effect of any special card - or maybe limited to repairs only.

RATING: 10
Nagyon kedvelem ezt a játékot!
Mi az utóbbi időben megpróbálunk mindig páratlan számú emberrel játszani és 5 főnél 2, 7 főnél 3, 9 főnél 4 szabotőrt alkalmazunk (magyarul mindig eggyel kevesebbet mint aranyásóból van). Így bár egy parányit egyszerűbb kitalálni ki a szabotőr és ki nem, de a szabotőröknek is mindig van esélyük győzelemre (pl. 5 játékosnál 4 az 1-ellen, vagy 7 játékosnál 5 a kettő ellen nagyon kevés a szabotőrök esélye).
Ha párosan vagyunk akkor alapból nem jó az elosztás hiszen pl. 6 játékosnál 3-3 szabotőr és aranyásó van, ami szinte garantálja utóbbiak sikerét, ha viszont 4 aranyásó és 2 szabotőr akkor az már az előbbieknek kedvez.

Elvesztem a részletekben, bocsi. :)
A lényeg hogy remek játék, főleg olyan társaságban ahol van több olyan aki szeret elméleteket gyártani és dumálni, csendes csapatnak nem nagyon (sőt egyáltalán nem) való.

Előnye még hogy 8 évesek is ugyanúgy tudnak játszani, és élvezni azt, bár sokszor belekavarnak, pl. letesznek egy lezárót mert elfelejtik, hogy el is lehet dobni. Persze ilyenkor mindenki azt hiszi, hogy ő a szabotőr és mindenkit megtéveszt, aztán a végén vannak nagy derülések, hogy mégis ki-kicsoda volt, szóval ha lehet gyerekekkel játszani, akkor ki ne hagyjátok! :) 

Nekem NAGYON BEJÖN ez a party- felvezetőjáték! :)

RATING: 7

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Great, casual fun in larger groups, especially as you play through a few rounds- first, as the inevitable new players get a handle on what's going on, and second, as the individual play style of players begins to emerge, despite their potential change in roles.  The inevitable Mafia-style paranoia comes out, particularly as players begin to discuss the board layout and potential plays, or beg for repairs.  

The breakage mechanism can leave you just sitting there with a dwindling hand if you can't convince someone to fix you, and there can be long gaps between your opportunities to play, but what's going on with the other players and the opportunity to contribute to the discussion (for good or ill) is entertaining enough not to make it boring.

In certain circumstances, usually when the Saboteurs are doing well, a deck inventory would be helpful: knowing that all the rockslides or appropriate tunnels are gone could help you decide whether the game is unwinnable, giving you the opportunity to cut it short and move on to the next round.

The ongoing scoring system is interesting, but not necessarily rewarding the best play from players, though as you develop further expertise as a miner manipulating the payouts can be an interesting tactic.

Strongly considering a look at the expansion- though there may be learning curve difficulties given that with large groups a few players will inevitably be new to the game.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
The players are dwarves digging to reach the gold that is hidden at one of three locations.  But one or more of the dwarves are saboteurs, trying to foil this plan.  Since the roles are hidden, it's fun trying to guess who the bad dwarves are OR trying to effectively sabotage the process without revealing your identity.  The game scales well from 3 to 10 players, but it's best when the saboteurs are not tremendously outnumbered.  The scoring system can lead to players having no chance of winning in the third (and final) round, so it's best to treat each round as though it were a single experience (kind of like a party game).
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7

RATING: 4
I want to like this, but it simply doesn't work for either me or my group. I suspect that we're simply not nasty enough to create an interesting and tense dynamic. There's virtually no incentive for the miners to squabble amonst themselves and there is only marginal benefit in the saboteurs keeping their identies secret (it's hard enough for the saboteurs already without them waiting longer to spring some kind of surprise). We also don't find that it's particularly 'fun' in the story-telling sense, as there is no clear narrative, sense of individual progress/personal achievement or any particular identification with your own 'miner' (who is at no time represented on the 'board'). I bought this game after researching on BGG but, unfortunately, it has turned out to be a big dissapointment.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.7458
Reminds me of kevan's Things game but working out who is the saboteur seems less essential and there's more of a need for the saboteur to show their hand.

I feel the game may be weighted towards the diggers - since useless cards can be played at the start (working back if needs be) a traitor that plays genuinely counter-productive moves can be easily spotted.

All a saboteur can do to screw the diggers is either lie about the location of the gold or play tunnels in sub-optimal places but the latter is too easy to see through once everyone's played a full round and gotten the hang of it.

When trying to decide who is lying and who isn't, the game can be a brilliantly tense affair. When on the brink of failure - with only a few cards in each player's hand - similar feelings arise.

A great game for getting to know folk better - seeing how folk lie and play a traitor reveals traits usually unseen.

Despite any arguable imbalance, the brevity and speed of game-state-change keeps it fun, light and interesting.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
I like the Saboteur game and it's one of my favorites, but I think it needs a few rule changes to make it more even between the good miners and the saboteur. The center gold card should be moved 2 more spaces away from the starting card. It takes 9 cards (sometimes 8 if you come from underneath), to get to the 2 outside gold cards but only takes 7 cards to get to the center gold card. It's too hard for the saboteur to stop the group if the gold is in the center. I also think the maximum number of times you should be able to sabotage someone (stop the saboteur) should be 2 or 3. It's hard enough to try to stop the other miners once the saboteur is discovered. By limiting the number of times you can stop someone with a broken lantern, pick axe or cart, it will give the saboteur a chance to win the game. The saboteur has never one in any of the games I have played. I came close 1 time but the last person left with any usable cards had the right path to get the gold.

RATING: 7
Jópofa kártyajáték, amit lehet gyerekekkel is együtt játszani. Gyakorlatilag a játékban törpék szerepébe bújunk, akik a földalatti járatok építésével próbálnak az aranyhoz eljutni. De ez még nem minden, néhány törpe bizony megpróbálja szabotálni a munkát, s ez adja a játék savát-borsát. Nem árt, ha van egy gyanúsítgató is a csapatban, aki kellőképpen hintába tudja ültetni a többieket, ezzel is emelve a játék hangulatát. Persze idővel kiderül ki(k) a szabotőr(ök), s onnantól bizony nehéz dolguk van. 4 fős játéknál eltértünk a szabálytól, ami azt mondja ki, hogy 4 törpe és 1 szabotőr közül választjuk ki titkosan a szerepünket (amit a forduló végéig titokban is tartunk), de így a szabotőrnek 3 törpe ellen nem sok esélye volt. Ezért úgy döntöttünk, hogy 3 törpe 2 szabotőr legyen a választandó szerepek között, ezzel növelve a szabotőrök esélyét. Nekünk ez így jobban bejött. Családi játéknak kiváló, s a kezdők is gond nélkül belevethetik magukat a vájár tevékenységbe, mert néhány egyszerű szabály meghallgatása után már jöhet is a móka. (2014.08.16.)

RATING: 7.5
Saboteur: Simple, Fast and Fun.   A very mellow ‘traitor’ game that can function as a good icebreaker.  The rules can be picked up quickly (be sure to point out the iconography rather than relying on the artwork on the cards) and this makes a great party game.  At some point it is inevitable that players who are saboteurs reveal themselves, but the best thing about this game is that those players are not out of the game in any way (as is the case in many of these ‘traitor’ games); they still have a 50/50 chance of winning by working with their fellow saboteurs and messing up the other players.  Even if the other players ‘break their tools’, saboteurs can STILL win, which may sound like the game tips in favour of the saboteurs, but I’ve seen an equally balanced number of situations when either saboteurs win or when the good-dwarves win, which is a good sign of a well-balanced game.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 9.25
This is one of three games I constantly have with me. It stays in my car because it has the ability to cure that empty space in any given night that begs to be filled with a fun boardgame. Its flexiblity with number of players, silly theme and player interaction make this a hit every time.

[b]6.8.09 Update:[/b] This game continues to be the best filler or game night opener that I own. And it never fails to draw people in and wet their appetite for more gaming! Rating moves up.

[b]3.12.10 Update:[/b] Played another rousing game with 10 players this time! Incredibly fun. Rating goes up again.

[b]5.9.10 Update:[/b] Officially added to my overall Top 10.

[b]1.7.14 Update:[/b] Played this for the first time in a long time, and man, it still rocks. Sitting around the table with 10 friends, hilariously accusing each other of sabotage, makes for great fun. I love this game!

RATING: 6
Superb!  A fantastic little game, very light and highly thematic.  I always play with the advanced rules (loyal dwarves with broken tools get no gold), put the center goal card an extra space away (to prevent a single tunnel card revealing two goal cards) and the saboteurs-in-cahoots rule (like Werewolf -- everyone closes their eyes, then the saboteurs open their eyes and see who each other are).

A phenomenal gateway game, a great introduction to hidden role games, a great filler ... what's not to like?

RATING: 6
This is fun basic filler, but I find the saboteur is usually quickly blocked with calamity cards for most of the game with little to do but discard, with everyone being limited to 1 new card per turn.  As such, 3 game rounds or more are required for final scoring which should hopefully balance this out.  

There is no real social deduction or 'traitor' aspect like in Shadows Over Camelot/BS Galactica/Dead of Winter.  The saboteur(s) should usually become evident relatively early, so success just comes down to the cards.  However players can still compete to receive more gold and block others (by using the optional screwage variant).  

I tend to think that an undiscovered saboteur should also receive some found gold, but this isn't in the rules.  There are a lot of mine sneak peek discovery cards and annoyingly, the results usually get divulged early on.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7
Despite the strange scoring mechanic (I think it needs a house rule to be more fair) it is an amusing but also kind of random game that scales well for 6 or more players. So far we liked it best when having 4 miners and 3 saboteurs in the team, so that the saboteurs really have a chance of winning some rounds. But the most fun parts of the game are the accusations based on questionable moves, delusions and trick-maneuvers. The later you reveal being a saboteur the more fun it can be. Hiding your identity as long as possible is actually the toughest part.

(As of [b]2[/b] plays) A co-op/traitor game in filler card game form. Despite the simplicity, there are heavy doses of wild accusations, unfounded suspicions and all-around squabbling, especially with the optional "Greedy Dwarf" rule in play. There is some concern that it is too hard to win as a Saboteur, although in most rounds it has come down to the last few cards. A great party game that can easily be taught to non-gamers.

[b]1 year verdict:[/b] This has not worked at all with my regular gaming group. It [i]did[/i] work quite well with a group of casual and non-gamers, but I'm not sure I'm justified in keeping it.

RATING: 8
Secret roles and bluffing like Bang, Werewolf, Shadows Over Camelot: a fun party card game that can handle up to 10 players, good for non-gamers.  Being on one of two secret teams is the most fun, and the scoring isn't really that important.  If the gold miners win too often, play it less as a team game, and focus on being the first gold miner to get the gold, or play the variant where gold miners who have broken equipment at the end of the game get no gold.  Try the [url=http://boardgamegeek.com/thread/141246]Werewolf Variant[/url], where the Saboteurs reveal their identity to each other before the game when the Gold-Diggers have their eyes shut.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Saboteur does one thing that most party games do not, or cannot do and that's make what is a game of accusation and paranoia accessible to a group of younger kids!  Normally party games aren't as accessible because you have to mentally process motives and possibilities whereas Saboteur delivers the party game vibe in a visual way.

The goal?  Get to the gold if you're good dwarves, if not; stop the good dwarves getting to the gold so you can have it all for yourself.  Play three rounds, whoever has the most gold at the end wins.

Players play cards in a tile-laying fashion to get to the end hidden treasure (two are duds, one is legit).  A player can do one of three things on their turn; place a tunnel card, break/repair people’s tools (tunnels can't be dug with broken tools) or discard and draw a new card.  The game’s tension is increased by an artificial timer of the deck, once all the cards are played or discarded, that is it.

This game is just as fun for adults and I personally believe it ups the suspicion factor over most games in a not overly confrontational way.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4
Don't play this with fewer that 5.  Better with more players.

We played with 3, and it is very difficult to actually win if you don't win as the Saboteur at least once.  Played again with 5 and then with 7 and it was much better, although the saboteur's won twice with 7, at it seemed like they had the advantage.

I liked that it is pretty short, and that you play it 3 times to get a winner.  The route building is also good.

What I don't like is that it is usually very obvious whether or not someone is the Saboteur or not.  There is no point in the regular players to do anything other than reach the goal.  They should dump their bad cards rather than play them.  The saboteur has to dump cards and just say that they have nothing and then at the last moment drop down a rockslide or broken tools.

Another thing I don't like is that you need a specific fix card for a specific broken tool.  I got hit with a broken tool, and never once got a fix card for it the whole game.  I would like the fix cards to fix any of the 3 broken tools.

I'm a fan of the possible variants where the middle card is pushed back one card, as well as the miners not getting a gold card if they have broken equipment.

RATING: 7
Aranyos partyjáték, ami nehezen kerülheti el, hogy összehasonlítsák a banggel, mivel ez is kártyás, sokan játszható, aránylag rövid, és itt is csapatokba osztva dolgoznak együtt, illetve egymás ellen az emberek, csakhogy a játék elején még senki se sejtheti, hogy ki-kivel van.
Egy játék után jobbnak érzem a bangnél, több benne csavar, kicsit nehezebb kitalálni, hogy ki kivel van. Az is jobban tetszett, hogy kevésbé rombolós, mint a bang, ahol gyakorlatilag, minden kijátszott kártyával valakinek ártasz. Itt lehet építve is rombolni, ami szintén jópofa lehetőség. A jutalomkártya-húzás elég nagy randomitást visz a játékba, de ahogy láttam ezt a kiegészítőben orvosolták. Kíváncsi vagyok, a kiegre, nomeg az alappal is kéne még jópárat játszani.
A legnagyobb előnyt a végére hagytam: mindenki egyből felfogta a szabályokat, és mindenkinek nagyon tetszett a játék, pedig nem gémer társaság volt. Egy partyjátéknál azt hiszem ez az egyik legfontosabb tényező.

RATING: 3
You rely too much on what you are dealt, and sometimes are rendered completely, permanently helpless early in the game through no fault of your own when you just can't draw the right cards.  I also wish there were more ways to communicate with others on your side. Any cooperation feels really haphazard.

I really never enjoyed this game and sold it in 2014 after not having played it for several years. Resistance and Mascarade are much better deduction games.

RATING: 5
This is a surprisingly good game.  The more people you have, the more saboteurs you potentially have, and the more fun the game becomes.  It doesn't even matter if the saboteurs are found out - the gold diggers can be ruthless about blocking other dwarves and preventing them from getting a share of the gold.  
Saboteurs are at a huge disadvantage, but it makes it all the more satisfying to win as one.  

I think my rating for this game suffers from the fact that I would be very reluctant to play this game with fewer than 6 people.  

My students love this game.  There is quite a bit of interaction and laughter when they find out they were hurting their own team and they don't quite understand the strategy, but they have a good time.  A 10-player round is over in less than 10 minutes, including set-up.

RATING: 6.3
To give the Saboteur an equal chance of winning use this official variant: good dwarves that have broken tools at the end of the round do not receive gold if their side wins... this adds a lot more to the meta game, as often quite innocent dwarves have their equipment broken because they have already won "too much gold".It makes it difficult to truly determine who the saboteur is..

Also in 6, 8 9 player games the Saboteurs could use a slight edge to improve their chances.  Try the Werewolf Variant suggested by Aaron Kurtz, where the Saboteurs secretly reveal themselves to each other at the start of the game.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
In the main game all gold-diggers (exept the saboteurs) get gold when someone finds it. The finder gets to pick the gold card first. In the official variant only the diggers who have all their gear intact can obtain the gold. The gold is distributed only amongst the diggers who could actually dig.

This turns the game a little bit interesting, as now not only the saboteur is using sabotage cards against everyone. In the normal game it was hard to "bash the leader" or make shure you have the most gold in the last round when being a digger. Now you can just brake the everyones stuff just before revealing the gold.
A couple of games have been a fight between the diggers, and loosing the gold even without a saboteur.. 

I prefere the variant over the main game because it allows a little bit of tactics into the three game rounds. As the gold-diggers are fighting amongs each other, the saboteur can start blocking the pathway for good.. Usualy at this point the diggers find a new harmony, atleast until the tresure is only one card away.. and stuff start mysteriosly breaking again

RATING: 6.5
A fun little hidden traitor tile laying game.  You are navigating a maze, and either trying to help find the gold or trying to hide the gold, by laying down maze-like cards to move a path to the gold.  It has a neat bluffing element to it, as even once people figure out what side you are on, you can fake them out in different ways.  

It doesn't seem to scale properly - we had seven players and the rounds where it was 4 / 3 were tense and interesting but one round where it was 5 / 2 we hit the gold so fast it wasn't even fun!

RATING: 5
[Initial Impression: 6]
A somewhat fun little game that can handle many players.  Unfortunately, the saboteurs are generally easy to identify (they have very little incentive to hide for long and can work together if there are several saboteurs), yet can be highly effective at stopping the miners.  In fact, with multiple saboteurs, the miners can only really win if they get very lucky card draws.  (This might be remedied if the ratio of valid to obstructed path cards were slightly higher.) Add in the fact that scoring is based on the number of gold icons on drawn cards (making it quite random - the winner will usually be a player who had the role of the saboteur the most).  This can be a fun, back-stabbing filler with the right group, but loses its luster relatively quickly.

RATING: 7
This game is for you if you want a quick pacing game that's a load of fun and that gives you a chance of being mischievous person (and enjoy it, mwahaahaha!!!). =-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
In my opinion, a more sophisticated version of Incan Gold/Diamant. The players, representing Dwarves, mine their way in through rock, in a race to get to hidden gold. Players alternate placing cards that depict the tunnels they mine, but they have to line up, sort of like that plumbing card game from childhood. The first dwarf to get to the treasure has first crack at the spoils, meaning less and less gold for the others clockwise to the first player. So, this is a mad dash to see who gets there first. Meanwhile, one of the dwarves may be the 'saboteur', who gets 4 pieces of gold for thwarting the mining, a la the traitor in Shadows Over Camelot, or the cylon in BSG. There are a number of 'screw your neighbor' cards which literally paralyze another dwarf, preventing him from playing cards other than cards the undo the attack cards.

It's great fun, with a lot more depth than Incan Gold/Diamant, because of the paranoia introduced by the traitor element, and also because of the pseudo-cooperative nature of the game. The players sort of need to help each other get to the treasure before the cards run out, while trying to figure out the saboteur and taking steps to neutralize his efforts. Its plus is that it can handle up to 10 (!) players, which is an extremely rare attribute, but the downside is that this game takes a bit longer than Inca Gold/Diamant. Also, it does not tap into the schadenfreude that is the hallmark of Inca Gold/Diamant. Which is better? It is a matter of personal taste, and how much effort you want to put into the game. For a quick, brainless, yet fun party filler, it's Inca Gold/Diamant. For a substantive filler, it's Saboteur.

RATING: 6
A simple introduction to the "hidden traitor" style of gaming that has been popular with several groups of new gamers. Much, MUCH shorter than something like BSG. There is technically some kind of score keeping mechanism but when we play all that matters is which side wins.

Because all virtually all play happens in the open it is much harder for the saboteurs to perform sabotage while remaining hidden. That is something BSG does much better. On the other hand, the deck is (relatively) small so there is less time for the miners to recover. I've played in games where the miners have technically lost with a dozen or so cards left to draw (because there is no remaining way to make the necessary connections) and that's a bit anticlimactic.

RATING: 10
Can any game get a group of people more animated?  Suspicion, and "random" acts that fool everyone else...  Saboteurs feuding and sabotaging one another, only to win when one reveals themselves to the miners who come to he aid of the other saboteur at a critical time...

Playing the alternative rules means that only miners with unbroken tools share the gold - which leads to the miners sabotaging one another, to the joy of the saboteurs!

Is this game a "filler", or the highlight of the evening?

RATING: 5
While the idea of combining Mafia-esque secret information with a map-building game sounds like a good idea in theory, in practice this one fell a little flat for me.  Unlike in Mafia, it's pretty much guaranteed that the Saboteur is going to be found out at some point (the game wouldn't last very long if they stayed hidden the whole time), and then it's basically a question of whether there's one or two Saboteurs.  If there's only one, it's practically impossible for him to stop the other players.  If there's two then they have a fighting chance.  Either way I didn't find the game to be very interesting.

RATING: 3
OWNED SINCE 2012
This is a fun game for me and my family to play (wife and 5 kids ages 5-11 years of age and up). It is light and quick, and can be fun. My smallest one even enjoys it, although he is not always helpful to his team, lol. My children 9 and up have a good understanding of the game and contribute to their side. The only problem with this game, and it is a huge problem, is that it is impossible for the saboteurs to act without being suspected. This is a sort game and there is no time to be subtle, or else you jeopardize losing. If do not act fast you will lose as a Saboteur. The problem is Saboteurs almost always lose because of it. I have tried many times to like this game, but it is just too hard to win as a saboteur and it is no longer fun to try. My dis still like this game, and they can play without parental supervision. So that is nice. But I do not enjoy playing this game. I would just prefer to play other games.

RATING: 4
Trying to stop the other players takes some trick in this game.  You really need to play like the miner for some of the game, and then sabotage them as they get closer, with less cards in the deck to stop you.  Plus if you make a move too quickly, everyone else will play their stopper cards on you.  It becomes a lot easier if there are multiple saboteurs in the same round, in that you can play off each other.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.5
This is a nice inexpensive game for up to 10 people, not many can handle that number well. The game moves along at a good pace and stays interesting enough throughout to hold your interest. 

The fun comes in from the hidden roles and trying to deduce who is who, it is also cooperative and competitive at the same time. There are two teams that compete against each other and you need to try and figure out who is who asap, once you do you can hinder opponents and help your teammates. Screwage also adds to the fun here as you hand out broken tools to the opposing team members. 

Recommended for 6 to 10 people.

RATING: N/A
Note there is also an official variant (which we always play), where good dwarves that have broken tools at the end of the round do not receive gold if their side wins... this adds a lot more to the meta game, as often quite innocent dwarves have their equipment broken because they have already won "too much gold".

It seems evident from the percentages that the Saboteurs have the least chance of succeeding in 3, 4, 6, and 9 player games. For the most part, this is corroborated by the results in this thread:
Post your results: Win record of Gold-Diggers vs Saboteurs
http://www.boardgamegeek.com/thread/164370

Especially in games with this number of players, perhaps the Saboteurs could use a slight edge to improve their chances. If you're finding that the Saboteurs don't have much hope of winning in 6, 8 9 player games, you should consider the Werewolf Variant suggested by Aaron Kurtz, where the Saboteurs secretly reveal themselves to each other at the start of the game. Details here:
Saboteurs know each other variant
http://www.boardgamegeek.com/thread/141246

RATING: 3
2012-04-12

Initial Rating: 5.0 (August 2010)

I love traitor mechanics, so I should like this game BUT I don´t. Not sure why but I don´t have any fun playing this and it is a shame because my game group like it fine. Perhaps I have an anti-chemistry with tile laying games (I also have an irrational hate for Carcassonne).

For me, the game is very light with low complexity (a minus for me), it has lots of meaningless decisions (either you have the right cards or not), an annoyingly high luck factor, paper thin theme and lots of accusations and “take that” moments (a plus for me but not enough). I feel the game is boring and I feel no desire to play it again (but probably will as many friends like it).

I have to say it seems the game is good enough to play with non-gamers and that’s about all the game has going for it.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4
Saboteur is a simple game that can be played entirely without communication. Hidden roles are given out at the start of the game, where players can either be a Dwarf or a Saboteur. The goal of the game is for the dwarves to reach the gold. Saboteurs try to prevent the dwarves from reaching the gold. Each turn, players play a card then draw a card. Cards are used to dig deeper into the mine, or to 'sabotage' other dwarves, gain information, etc. First dwarf team to the gold wins.

The game is not as 'social' as some others (i.e. The Resistance) and does not contain enough depth in gameplay to be compelling in the long term. However, for a quick, light, somewhat fun (occasionally funny, but not as much as I expect) game, you cannot go wrong* with Saboteur. 

*Unless you have been deliberately going the wrong way the whole time, in which case, you are going the right way.

RATING: 9
This game is a the best ice breaker/filler game I've played. It's easy to setup and you can explain everything within five minutes. The secret roles make the game interesting, and best of all it can handle up to 10 people.

I don't think this is the kind of game that you'd want to play over and over again (Bang! is probably better for that), but as a light filler game, with a very fast learning curve (which is lacking in Bang!) I think it's perfect and brings both gamers and non-gamers to the same table.

RATING: 7
Nagyon szórakoztató kártyajáték. Tetszik, hogy nem feltétlenül derül ki, hogy ki a szabotőr, főleg, ha valaki, akiről eddig azt hitted, hogy aranyásó, valami furcsát játszik ki. Meg tudja keverni a dolgokat. Fordítva is igaz, mert van, amikor egyértelműnek tűnik, hogy ki a szabotőr, aztán pedig valamelyik akciója után elbizonytalanodik az ember.
Véleményem szerint a szabotőrnek könnyebb dolga van, de eléggé kiegyensúlyozott a játék, mert az aranyásóknak is jó lehetőségük van nyerni.

A szabályok kicsit bő lére eresztve vannak megfogalmazva, szerintem lehetne rajta egyszerűsíteni, egyértelműsíteni.

Azt viszont egyáltalán nem értem, hogy ha már a doboz magyar, a játékleírás magyar, akkor a Saboteur szó miért nem szerepelhet magyarul a kártyákon? Azért a pár lapért feleslegesnek tartották? Természetesn nem zavaró, csak furcsa.

Megjegyzés: Játszottam 9 (meg én voltam a tizedik) 11 éves gyerekkel, és teljesen le voltak nyűgözve, imádták a játékot. azért ez sok plusz pont a javára! :D

RATING: 5
We primarily play with 3 so this game didn't really work well for us.  I'm not sure I'd like it much better with more either though.  Ultimately the tunnel placement is much much more fun in a game like Karuba so that leaves the other elements.  Card play itself is a bit dull as its usually obvious what to play if your a miner.  Plus your hand gets cluttered up with stuff you really can't use if you don't know who the saboteur is or if there isn't one so your mostly just waiting to draw the needed card.  As the saboteur it's more interesting but I wouldn't say exciting.  And the whole broken/fix tools mechanic is a straight rip of the classic Mille Borne game which I loathe these days. I don't really care for the random draw of the gold cards when the miners win either. I do know a lot changes with the expansion but I bought this in 2016 new so apparently the publishers still think this game works as-is for the specified player count.  I'm not going to sync more money into a just ok game at this point.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
I have been changing my thoughts on this one for quite some time and, after quite a bunch of plays with different people, as well as different number of players, I've consolidated an opinion: it's silly, yes, it's light, yes, but it's fun.

The key mechanism of this one is the hidden roles. It also is its main drawback, as the game can be played wrong, tactically speaking. Being a "good" dwarf doesn't mean that you have to reach the gold at all costs: if you get the last pieces of gold, you'll be earning one while the first dwarf gains three or four. "Good" dwarves not only must try to reach the exit, they must try to get there first. The game is further enhanced if you play with a variant in which only the "good" dwarves with all their equipment intact get any gold. If "good" dwarves aren't trying to stop each other, if they aren't forming gangs, if they aren't divided in teams, you are playing the game in the way it's not particulary fun.

But if "good" dwarves start getting competitive, then Sabouteur becomes a very fun light card game that's great for large groups.

Rating: :star::star::star::star::nostar:
Optimal number of players:
:thumbsup:8~10
:thumbsdown:3~5

RATING: 7.5
Players take on the role of dwarves. As miners, they are in a mine, hunting for gold. Suddenly, a pick axe swings down and shatters the mine lamp. The saboteur has struck. But which of the players are saboteurs? Will you find the gold, or will the fiendish actions of the saboteurs lead them to it first? After three rounds, the player with the most gold is the winner.

With the help of Dwarf Cards, the players are assigned their role: either miner or saboteur. The roles are kept secret- they are only revealed at the end of the game.

RATING: 8
This has been a staple of mine on BoardGameArena, along with Puerto Rico and Jaipur. I actually stumbled on Saboteur as I was bored waiting for Puerto Rico lobbies to open, or anyone to join my game, but man did this game exceed all expectations. It's a hidden-role game, and before you audibly groan I'll have you know I like hidden-role games, as evident by my interest in Cosmic Encounter, One Night Ultimate Werewolf, and Resistance/Avalon. But what's great about this game is that it combines this style with Carcassonne, where you're building a path to try and find the gold, unless you're the 'Saboteur' and you're trying to stop them from finding the gold. There's a bunch of cards to help you get there and make the path, and there's cards that stop people from building paths. There's cards to look at where the gold is, and cards to stop others from looking. There's cards to sabotage the path, and cards to stop that from happening, etc. Lots of options.

What really appeals to me about this game is that it's cheap, light, and while it is luck based it has one of the most intriguing game mechanics I have seen in a game as cheap as it is. This could very well have been $50 more and come with tiles and other crap, maybe a board, maybe some fancy artwork, but instead they made the game as simply as possible so that it fits in a small box very easily, can play on a small amount of space, and can be bought for extremely cheap, even at MSRP (maybe not extremely cheap, but still cheap in terms of board games). I can't wait to get this game and play it with my friends, and while none of them have played it they should pick it up easily and have a good time.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.3
This is a clever little game that serves excellent as a filler (have only tried it from 4 to 7 players and it scales well within this intervall). It defenitely grows with the number of play (between 10 and 15 so far) since the interaction and competitioin between miners grow for each play. 
In earlier games it was more clear cut divided sabuteurs against miners, now blocking and miners (and releasing them) is frequently part of the deduction and gambling tactics to be the among the ones who reach the gold nugget and are allowed to share the treasure. 
Saboteur roles also get more clever in hiding there role till it is necessary to reveal it to prevent miners from reaching their goal. 

All this also increases the fun of the game tremendously. It has really high replaybility since the distribution of roles differ from each play as do the the order the tunnels are placed. Of course it does not contain any deeper strategy but is very much up to tactical decissions and deduction. 

It plays quickly 20-30 minutes and almost always make me leave the gaming session with a smile on my face (no matter the outcome of the game).

RATING: 6
I haven't cracked this nut yet. It seems too difficult to win against whoever lucks into not ever being a saboteur, and too hard to win as the saboteurs in general -- but it's a pretty fun game.

I like the tension of not knowing who's who, and the pleasure of being a saboteur and figuring out who your buddy is. It plays quickly, but doesn't end too soon; a nice balance.

The biggest downside is the lack of a board -- it needs a board, as the careful positioning of the cards is integral to the game. As it doesn't come with one, we use a 3x3 square of felt to keep the cards from wiggling around too much.

A combination of annoyance at the components and less-than-fond memories of its gameplay, I sold it.

RATING: 8
Help your team, sabotage the opposition, bluff one or both sides, or simply play randomly to confuse people.  

A very fun game, in which players are digging for gold and there are one or more hidden traitors in their midst who are trying to sabotage things.

The hidden traitor mechanic can lead to some excellent results. Like misleading a saboteur to make them think that you are a saboteur too when you're really working for the good guys. Or playing randomly just to mess with people.

Plays really quickly once people have the mechanics down. Very easy to teach and very fun.

RATING: 9
It took me a good few months to actually get this game to the table.  I thought oh, another card game...oh, tile laying...sounds boring.  It wasn't until the awesome guys in Australia showed me how to play this game, and how fun it was, was I able to bring this out.  

This is such an awesome, portable, fun, game that scales well.  Play with 4-10 and it's still fun.  It plays quickly, and it makes everyone laugh.  Such an easy game to teach, and I think this game might be one that'll draw people into the hobby.

RATING: 7.5
I didn't like this game at first.  In fact, the likelihood of the Saboteur(s) winning seemed so small that it almost felt broken.  Then a friend mentioned he ALWAYS plays with the following two variants: 1. The center goal card is 1 additional space away (8 instead of 7 - the top and bottom are still 7); 2. If the non-saboteurs win, they only get to share in the gold if they have no remaining broken tools at the end.  Rule 2 is huge -- this causes the good dwarves to turn on each other towards the end and can make it harder to identify the saboteur.  It also keeps people from piling all their attack cards on the suspected saboteur - they want to save some to help get richer.  Much more fun, much better game now.  I also recommend playing with at least 5 to get the potential for 2 saboteurs.

RATING: 7
(Only played with 4 people, so far.)  A neat little quick game that has some interesting player interactions.  Easy to get into and play.  Once you discover that the game is really not about the many "good" dwarves versus the "bad" dwarf, but actually each "good" dwarf can hose the other dwarves to his advantage, it gets a lot more interesting.  You then fight the   card stack AND the saboteur.  Perhaps if the payoffs were a little more dramatic, that would encourage this style of play, but I can see how you might want to just "be nice" with each other.  Not being nice is a lot more fun though!  "Bang!" is superior, but this one is a nice change of pace for a large crowd.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
Game in a Nutshell: Play as gnomes digging in a mine for gold. While some players are working their way to the gold, a secret few are working against their efforts.

Played as: 7,8,9,10 player

Played with: Vanilla, and With Saboteur 2

Pros: Best game I’ve played out there for getting people up out of their seats and pointing fingers and shouting accusations (always in good spirit). The interaction is ace. I love the crafty grin on the face of a hidden saboteur when they slyly (or not so slyly) reveal themselves by laying (or slamming) down a card that blocks the path of the hard working gnomes. The game matures like a fine wine as players get more plays in and play with a finer finesse. Overall, it’s a light, quick to play, easy to introduce game that fits a decent sized group.

Cons: Even though I haven’t had this problem yet, player interaction games often depend on the players at the table.  If you have the type of people who want to sit in quiet contemplation, this game won’t go over well. Also, it’s not going to satisfy people looking to have a lot of control in a game, as the winner never seems like it is the one who played the best game and hardly matters very much. I wouldn’t want to overplay this game; it’s a blast to bring out on occasion, but could easily go stale when played too much. 

Other: This game just flat trumped Bang; at least with a bigger group (6-10 players). It fits that same niche but lacks player elimination, and gains a clearer goal with a far quicker pace.  I think it’s important that players understand the skill in this game comes more from playing the players, not playing the cards. I've enjoyed this more as an experience then a game, but I believe the expansion helps bring more of a game-y element into the mix. 

Best Use: Great game for a large-ish group with all types of players (though the rowdier the better).

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Very enjoyable and simple role deduction game with a traitor mechanic. I'm usually always up to play this game especially since the saboteur and miner roles are balanced fairly well (miners should play greedily because of the scoring rules so anyone that hurts you is not necessarily a saboteur). The only issue I have is that scoring is played in 3 rounds which means that if you have an awful 2 rounds then you usually have no chance of a comeback. I would suggest for a more appropriate way of averaging scores to go up to 5 rounds instead, though 3 rounds is perfect for a length of a game so it's up to the group.

RATING: 4
I disliked this game right off the bat when I first played it a few years ago. Played it again recently, and my opinion has not changed. There's just no way to play with any subtlety as a saboteur, at least not if you want to have any chance of winning. So either the saboteurs underplay their hands and just silently lose while hoping for the perfect time to strike (which never happens), or they out themselves early, and by the 3rd or 4th round, it's stinkingly obvious who the saboteurs are, and the game just turns into a boring tug-o-war between the miners and the saboteurs, which the miners will usually win just because there's more of them, and it's easy to cripple the saboteurs by breaking their equipment. The end result is that every game of Saboteur is just way too predictable, paint-by-the-numbers, and completely lacking in any sort of tension.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5.5
Are your friends sabotaging your attempts to dig gold? Are they telling the truth about what their map has revealed? A game of secret identities, with two important differences from The Resistance: (1) the saboteurs don't know who the other saboteurs are (or even if there are any other saboteurs) and (2) actions are largely transparent, so it's much harder to shift blame and sow doubt as a saboteur. A bit too luck-based, but a fun diversion.

RATING: 7
Hard to find games that work with 6+, are language independent, don't have player elimination, are easy to teach, and have more than one thing going on.  Saboteur manages all of that.  It isn't amazing or anything, but to quote the old Mac ads, "it just works." A little bit of bluffing, a little bit of puzzle (fitting the maze pieces together), a little bit of strategy (e.g., when to play a particular card), and it doesn't overstay its welcome.  Price to experience, a very solid game.

RATING: 7
This is a card game with hidden roles.  Saying that that makes it "Bang! Lite" is like saying that Carcassonne is "Tigris & Euphrates Lite" because it's a tile-placing game with wooden bits. RATING: 4
i really wanted to like this game, it's simple, it does not take forever, the theme is fun but the ending to each round is really not well thought. for me, picking the miner kills the game almost instantly. essentially everybody who is a miner wants to place the last card since that enables you to pick most of the gold (other miners than pick in the order they were seated). that is supposed to create tension and you have to decide between helping your team and maybe receive some gold, or let the saboteurs have it. the problem is, in games with larger groups everybody keeps 2 cards distance from the gold, so when you decide that you will place a card that helps your team, player going after you will take it. this means that the person who helped the most in reaching your common goal with get the least out of it. (or maybe i am wrong and this game is really some deep philosophical message about how life works according to the designers :)) in the end, nobody wants to do that, everybody stalls in the final phase and that is just not fun.

RATING: 6.5
心得:壞人難獲勝，主要是一開始沒理由禁止其他人，好人不內鬨難贏
但是最後是比金塊最多的獲勝，又跟總抽到的金塊牌有關，
運氣成分應該是較大的陣營遊戲。
規則:
◆三人遊戲：1個妨礙者與3個挖金人 
◆四人遊戲：1個妨礙者與4個挖金人     
◆五人遊戲：2個妨礙者與4個挖金人     
◆六人遊戲：2個妨礙者與5個挖金人    
◆七人遊戲：3個妨礙者與5個挖金人
◆八人遊戲：3個妨礙者與6個挖金人
◆九人遊戲：3個妨礙者與7個挖金人
◆十人遊戲：所有的矮人卡
● 依遊戲人數發予每位玩家手牌。
   3-5名玩家：6張
   6-7名玩家：5張
   8-10名玩家：4張
*形成一個5*9的卡牌陣列，3-1放起始通道，9-1,3,5放三張蓋的終點卡
*輪流做一個行動 之後抽一張卡
出坑道卡 前面不能有阻礙卡，要能合法相連到場上其他坑道卡
出行動卡
棄牌略過 蓋著棄一張

*障礙卡同種在一個人前只能一張
遊戲在以下兩種情況立即結束：
1.若翻出的終點卡上出現的是金塊，由好人獲勝。
2.當所有玩家手牌用盡或是無牌可出，由壞人獲勝。

*好人獲勝，抽出金塊卡張數等於玩家人數，在所有好人*逆時鐘*分
*當10人遊戲時，只會發放9張金塊卡。
*1名壞人：合計4塊金塊的金塊卡。
*2-3名壞人：合計3塊金塊的金塊卡。
*4名壞人：合計2塊金塊的金塊卡。
*遊戲進行三次，由金塊最多的玩家獲勝。

RATING: 6

Family Game. Group Game (up to 10 players).

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.5
A nice secret identity game, where good players are trying to build a path to find gold and the bad players are trying to secretly sabotage said path. The deck acts as the timer and if the path is incomplete when the deck is empty the saboteurs win. Though it's a little easier to figure out who the traitors are when compared to games like one night werewolf or the resistance, the difference is that knowing is not always enough to win. 

The good team must still work semi-cooperatively together and actively target the traitors. Generally though, this game often falls over in groups I play with, because people do not realize that this game is supposed to be played semi-coperatively (not fully cooperatively). 

If you are on the good team, it's not just about your team winning, it's just as important that YOU are the person in the team to actually REACH the gold. People who get to the gold FIRST generally get more gold than their team mates who may have helped out along the way.

RATING: 6.5
A cute game. You have to build a trail to find the gold which can be one of three cards (which are hidden). Yet there is a catch, one of the players may be a saboteur, trying to stop you from getting the gold. Also, the player you places the last card that reaches the gold, gets an extra reward. The problem is that being the saboteur is very hard. It is too obvious and there are too many cards so you almost always get to the gold. Your only chance as the saboteur is if the players fight for the last card placement. Still fun and plays with any number from 3 to 10 players.

RATING: 5
I've only had a 4-player game so that may twist my opinion a bit. The game was an ok time-consumer but nothing more. You get cards and on your turn either play one or discard one, in the end of your turn you draw one card.

There's also three different ways to harm the play of the others. Back-stabbing isn't a rule though, but still it's something you just have to do to your suspects. The problem with 4 players is that there is only one saboteur, so your efforts to bluff are mainly in vain.

A little too much Bangy to my taste.

RATING: 9

It may even trump The Resistance, because it offers a little more strategy besides metagaming.

RATING: 8
Quick card game with secret roles that plays up to 10 players, and actually plays well with many players. Can be great fun with a group that knows each other well, as the players try to deduce which of them may be on each of the 2 sides.

NOTE: Rules aren't clear on this point, but designer has confirmed that any card placed in the map must be able to trace a path back to the start card. So for example, a cave-in must be repaired before the path can continue. See...
http://www.boardgamegeek.com/thread/24487

NOTE: There is a Greedy Dwarf variant which helps to add some competition between non-saboteurs since only players with no broken tools when the gold is found receive a share of the points.

NOTE: A possible variant to avoid 2 goal cards being revealed by a single crossroads path card - simply place the middle goal card one space further away from the start.

SOME GOOD VARIANTS HERE...
http://boardgamegeek.com/thread/242686

RATING: 6
Mining game which "claims" to play up to 10, but even with first playing with 7 was too chaotic. Not only are you at the mercy of the Mille Bornes style "take that" from opponents but also card draws can be frustrating. Update: Second playing with 7 has grown on me, as the importance of determining who's who becomes apparent. Have now played with a group of 8 who I've introduced Werewolf to in the past, and this was a more satisfying outing, with one round very quick and one down to the wire with 2 wins by the Saboteurs. An example of group dynamics and familiarity of game concept influencing the experience.

RATING: 4
This game features hidden roles, sabotage, and some fairly simple gameplay. With four players there's a possibility each round that one person is a saboteur, and it seems to me that there may be hidden roles, but you sort out who is the traitor pretty much as soon as a conspicuously suspicious move is made. Then you just try and sandbag the traitor, and hope that you're first to the gold so you get a better share. Vos was a miner in the the first round, and a successful traitor in the second, and then we stopped. I think the game has more (but possibly less) potential with higher player counts adding more saboteur possibilities, but I'll have to take a look at the rules.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5.25
I admit, I am a bit spoiled when it comes to games involving a traitor, as I had the pleasure of being introduced to the mechanic through the brillian BSG. However, the prospect of a light filler/opener game including a traitor (Saboteur) intrigued me. The game plays simple and fast, as expected but the traitor mechanic is not very slick. Being the traitor and staying undetected is almost impossible and the "suspence" and "accusing" usually stops after a few turns, once it is settled who the traitor is, what follows is just a game of luck, because however holds the right cards, wins, all tactics and strategy is pretty much thrown overboard ( not that there was awfully much in the first place, but at least the traitor is thinking about how to remain undiscovered). We had fun, but it must be said that my gamegroup us very lively and as such we threw around quite a few accusations, but with the "wrong" kind of people, the gameplay can be rather stale. Again, a nice filler which is good in the face of a lacking alternative, but other than that, the novelty wears flat rather quickly.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
One of my very favourite 'simple' games. 

While it's true that the game 'plays itself' a little bit, this game still distils a lot of judgement and some nice squinting  "which player(s) is the traitor?" into a short and very portable format.

It's always quick enough not to outstay its welcome.

I'm a big fan, too, of how it gently encourages even allies to seem suspicious thanks to the way scoring happens. Only half of the battle is to be on the wiinning side - you'll still want to be THE dwarf who finds the gold, as that'll likely get you a better score. So you might delay playing your most helpful cards etc until YOU can use them rather than unil your team can.

It's no 'The Resistance: Avalon', which also comes in a small box and provides a superlative "who's the traitor?" experience. But The Resistance Avalon is longer and almost headache-inducingly meta/nuanced, whereas Saboteur is just a nice friendly game that you can play while talking about the weather.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
This game is perfect for larger groups wanting to warm up with a light game before moving on to something heavier.  With the right crowd you can get lots of laughs playing this game.  The right crowd would be people who delight in taking a role and playing it to the hilt without divulging to others who they are. When I play, I remind my group: "We're dwarves! Saboteur or not, we're greedy for gold! We'll do anything possible to get there first!"

If you like playing Werewolf or Mafia, you'll enjoy this game too.

I've seen others observe the potential for runaway leaders, and this has been my experience. But hey, this is a light game that can be played in a few minutes.  I just can't get that worked up about that problem.

That said, I do find one thing about the game irritating: why aren't the cards square?!  This one thing has bothered more people who play the game than anything else. Square cards can also help with the incongruities when trying to fit the 3 goal cards to the existing map.

The game's a lot of fun for the price. If you're looking for a crowd pleaser and want something different than Werewolf or Mafia, give this one a look.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
:thumbsup: Saboteur handles the hidden traitor mechanic in a really clever way. All players, even the non-saboteurs, are exhibiting traitorous behaviour because they want to be the first to reach the gold in order to score the most points and win. This makes it a bit less obvious who the real saboteur is.
:thumbsup: It’s a game that’s fast and fun at a high player count.
:thumbsup: Most people want to play again right away.

----

:thumbsdown: In the lower players counts, it’s hard to be the saboteur. Unless you’ve got a group of players who understand what makes this game shine and act like a trio (or quartet, or…) of shady dwarvers regardless of what their role card tells them.
:thumbsdown:
:thumbsdown:

RATING: 8
An excellent light, quick card game, but probably one that requires the right group. The bluffing and doublethink aspects work very well. Probably the only traitor / negotiation / take that game I've encountered that would be suitable for sensitive petals.

A lot of the comments for this game say that it's difficult for the saboteurs to beat the miners. I think the idea is that some of the miners can help the saboteurs in order to bash the leader. It's not a team game; he with the most nuggets wins. Best with more players, but quite playable with 4.

RATING: 7
Lightweight card game that plays fast with simple rules, but has plenty of room for strategy.  The traitors (saboteurs) can be difficult to identify, especially towards the end of a round when everyone starts breaking other players' equipment to get more gold.  Being the saboteur is intense and can be nerve-wracking with fewer players.  You can pick the right time to reveal yourself and just start trashing things, or you can be more subtle and sew doubt and start accusing others of being the saboteur.  The art is clean and effective, but nothing special.

Some others are saboteurs that will try to avoid that, for an unexplained and crafty reason.  Players can cave, demolish, see maps, destroy tools and repair them to fulfill their objective.  Very good choice for large groups.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 1.5
Kinda reminds me on Panic Station, meaning the game is mix of hidden roles and on the table play, this time in the version of building tunnels. Problem is similar, namely that roles are easy to figure out. Add on top of it is a pretty simple yet very strong take that element (locking other players) and there's not really much to do against it. A lot of it seems to be based on luck - which group gets which of the strong cards, how much saboteurs are present (+1 or -1). A part we haven't figured out yet is how egoistically should the good guys play (blocking persons from winning as they'd get the best cards). 

The game looks beautiful, is simple to pick up and is really affordable. However take that element of it is a bit clunky, slows the game down and frustrating at times. As for the story and narrative, yes it's there, but Panic Station does it better. 

EDIT: currently it falls down. Take that mechanic here just feels like stalling and there are many more exciting hidden role games out there.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
In Saboteur, players seemingly work together to mine a route towards the gold deposit, but a traitor or two among them complicates matters. It's a quick and simple tile-laying game with a dash of treachery involved as action cards can be played to rein in players perceived to be on the opposing team.

My main reservation regarding Saboteur is that the capability to manoeuvre around in the game is largely dictated by the cards in a player's hand. A hand full of dead ends can easily lock a player out for the round as he desperately tries to convince others that [i]really[/i], he is indeed on the good side. As far as hidden role deduction games go, Saboteur is just alright, but outclassed by games like [thing=41114][/thing].

RATING: 7
OK, first of all if you put aside all of its flaws the game is fun.  That's the thing to remember.  That said I sure wish there was a little more game here.  I enjoy this so much that I'm trying to find a balance to it so that the the winner isn't the player that draws the most gold digger cards.  Out of the box it is near impossible for the Saboteurs to win.

I was getting better results with the deposits 8 spaces away, now I think that the center deposit needs to be 9 spaces away and the two sides 8 spaces.  I also feel that there needs to always be one extra Saboteur thrown into the initial card mix.

Even still, it may be too tough for the Saboteurs...


If I can get it working I think it is a fantastic light map making card game where not everyone is working for the same side.  There is a traitor in our midst.  The payoff is high if you are the traitor, but sadly it is just too tough to pull off. With 5 players if there is only one traitor the game is impossibly stacked against him.  

Regardless, even if you are losing the tension is high, to complete the tunnel or sabotage it. I'm not sure if this game has any depth, but it brings quite a bit of fun.  Highly addictive gem that if it can be made to work it makes for a much better replacement to Bang.

RATING: 9
I really like this small card game with hidden factions. If you're a dwarf, you have to be careful about placing the tunnels, if you're a saboteur, you try to make subtle obstacles in making the tunnels. You make a turn where practically it means that if you destroy the cross, it's very hard to replace it. But at first it doesn't look like you spoil the play of dwarves. Also you can talk your oponents out of thinking you're the saboteur. And it's quick. Love it. The only problem is when you get together with players who play clearly like a saboteur, but are actually dwarves. Usually other dwarves destroy his lamp, pickaxe and everything and you end up loosing as a dwarf. But even despite that I still love this game, wish it would be played more often in our group.
