=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
This game reminded me a lot of Mille Bornes but with a hidden role mechanic.  In this game players are each dwarves mining for gold.  Some dwarves are saboteurs however and they never want the other dwarves to find the gold.  Each turn a player plays one of the cards from their hand.  Most of these are path cards that they are trying to use to build a path to the gold.  Others break other players' equipment, repair broken equipment (these two reminded me the most of Mille Bornes), look at the goal cards to find the one with gold on it, or remove placed path cards.

Either the dwarves make it to the gold and each non-saboteur is rewarded or the deck runs out and the saboteurs are rewarded.  You do this for three rounds and the dwarf with the most gold wins.

The hidden role mechanics are kind of shallow.  There isn't a whole lot of meaningful opportunity to bluff in this game so the saboteurs are discovered reasonably early.  As a social game it is fine though, you do have a few decisions since you have a hand of 4 or more cards to work with each turn.  The one really crappy thing though is (and this is resolved in the expansion I believe) if you have equipment broken and never draw the appropriate repair card you can spend many turns just twiddling your thumbs.  This is exacerbated if you are the only saboteur since people will pile up tons of broken stuff on you to try and knock you out of the game completely.  Not very fun in that situation.

RATING: 7
A traitor mechanic game where the play isn't centralized around determining who the traitor is, as much as it is tunneling as a team towards a common goal, with the traitors covertly and overtly trying to block.  Furthermore, as there are only a set number of treasure cards to be awarded if the diggers get to the goal, players can selfishly wait for the perfect opportunity to strike.  A very clever game, and with expansions that make teams, or narrow it down to a two-player game, this has a lot of versatility.  Plus each of the three rounds play fast, so it makes for a great filler.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
Hey look, it's "Shadows Over Camelot Lite"!  It is another co-operative game with the twist of one or more potential "traitors" in your midst.  It even has a theme that fits quite well with the game play (rare for a card game!).  Of course, what really makes it interesting is that secret role selection, which means you are initially not sure who is working for you and who is working against you, much like real life dwarf gold miners.  The cards have fun illustrations (I actually like the backs of the cards better than the fronts) and the game comes in a very small, very portable box that can be slipped into your pocket and taken pretty much anywhere (except under water), even into a real gold mine.  The rules are simple and the game play is quick and deadly.  But, similarly to "Citadels" (another card game I enjoy), you'll need to get at least 3-4 players together in order to get the most out of this game.  And I recommend playing at least 5 rounds in order to decrease the chance of a player winning due to a lucky card draw or two.  "Hey! That's My Fish!" is still my favourite "filler" game, but with 5 or more players, this is the one to "dig" out.  Game design: 4.5/5  Personal enjoyment: 3/5  Total: 7.5/10

RATING: 6.5
[Amigo Spiele 2004 Edition] {Party, gold digging; secret identity, partnership, tile-laying; optimal 7-10p} A nice and interesting party game.  Full of player interaction, intrigues and sabotage. It is usually easy to find out gold diggers and saboteurs. Therefore, some ground rules must be stated that players are not allowed to clearly tell which card they have.

Decisions are limited in Saboteur because of hand limit and events. I think 'rock-fall' is too powerful in some cases, esp. for the Saboteurs. Usually, the team holding the 'rock-fall' cards wins. Nevertheless, a good teamwork could increase win chance.

It's not clear in the rule about dividing nuggets when the Saboteurs win.  I choose this way to make the card distribution more even
- 4 saboteur: 3, 3, 2, 2, 1, 1
- 3 saboteur: 3, 2, 2, 1, 1
- 2 Saboteur: 3, 2, 1

RATING: 8
Easily accessible and enjoyable game, taking on the hidden role of a dwarf or saboteurs searching for Gold. 

People always want to be the Saboteur but it require many plays to play well and win.

Harder still is managing the co-operation of the the dwarves hands. Most players start by setting up their fellow dwarves to complete the maze but soon realise that allies get more reward points than they do. 

You then need to advance in skills so that you scupper your allies by breaking their tools so they cant complete the maze. Only then does the game come to fruition in the way that it was designed to. 

Not many people reach this level of understanding or or can cope with this level of double crossing required against friend and foe.

It's a great game when it works though.

RATING: 3
This is a semi-cooperative game.  You're miners trying to dig a path to the gold.  However, there may be one or more saboteurs who is trying to hinder everyone else.  The game is played over 3 rounds, so the saboteurs are randomly drawn before each round.

My main criticism of this game is the lack of social interaction during play.  No communications is allowed and you have to deduce who may or may not be on your side.  The silent playing of cards during each round until it is over just turns me off.  I play games to socialise and this game hinders the social aspect of gaming.

Final thoughts: Some other party games work better than this.

RATING: 7
An ok traitor like game, I really like Avalon and Deception Murder in HK much much better than this though.  While Avalon and Deception allow you to really mislead players provided you don't give up your bluff, saboteur really just involves playing cards, which means it is more about the luck of your draw and how long until you want to play the first bad card on the other players.  Once you do, you are immediately singled out.  Unlike so many other traitor games where you can get into a grey area where people start accusing you and back your way out, you pretty much go from completely innocent to completely guilty in one card play.  I like the idea, but there are such great deception games out there that this really doesn't seem like it needs to be on my shelf.

RATING: N/A
3-10
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4
I've always liked the idea of this game: you collectively build a path, but some people are trying to divert the path and hinder the other players.

There are a couple of issues, though. You're supposed to deal out the hidden roles and have one role leftover, so there could be one fewer saboteur. You need to houserule that the saboteurs are all in play, otherwise they have almost no chance of winning. The scoring also doesn't work. Starting with whoever ended the game, you start drafting cards that are worth 1-3 points. The people last in line will always just get one point based arbitrarily on seating order.

It seems like Saboteur would be perfect for today's audience with social deduction games being so prevalent. I would like to see this system tweaked and modernized a little (maybe add more roles), but as it stands it's just not a very good game.

RATING: 7

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
1/8/12 - I bought this game for variety's sake. My family and friends enjoy The Resistance so much that I felt it would also work, while switching things up a bit. It's a good little game, but it was my mistake to think it would be anything like (or as good) as The Resistance. 

The biggest difference between the two is that in The Resistance, a spy character absolutely MUST play out the lie until the bitter end of the game. In Saboteur, the lie will only really last a couple rounds for some, and for the rest of the saboteurs, it rarely last longer than half the game. At certain points early on, it just becomes optimal for the Saboteur to make an obviously sabotaging move and give himself up, in order to best his chances for the win.

The game is still good. And I plan to keep it, BUT, only because the the younger kids in my family often BEG to play The Resistance. And in all honesty, The Resistance doesn't work well with children who don't understand fully the interactions and lying element of The Resistance. Enter Saboteur for those moments.

Suitability for Travel:

I have a 1 to 5 scale for four categories (1 is worst, 5 is best) in order of importance:

Portability (the less luggage space the better) - 5
Footprint (the less table space when playing the better) - 3
Scalability (the wider range of player counts the better) - 5
Learnability (the easier to teach non-gamers the better) - 4


Overall - 4

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Saboteur is a pretty good little game. I tried to read the rules to get a feel for the game before it came out, but the rules don't tell you squat about what the game is like. 

This game is like werewolf or bang, and the rules are just a means to an end. If you are a saboteur, you are trying to play bad cards or shift blame to other players and act like you are being forced to by the luck of the draw. If you are a regular player, you are trying to reach the gold hidden in one of three locations, and of course, try to find the saboteur and shut them down. 

The game plays very quickly, and normally consists of several rounds, but that makes it a good filler because you can adjust the length of the game to match, and no-one has to wait very long for you to finish.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4
I enjoyed my play, but there's just so little there.  With 8 players (considered one of the best numbers to play with), it is utterly trivial for the saboteurs to win every time there's 3 (67%).  There would need to be ~1-4 more horizontal pathways for the miners to have any chance in this situation.

The gold card mechanic is also terrible if you're playing a setup where it's possible for the miners to win.  Setting up the next player to complete a connection is horrifying: you're expecting about 1 nugget in this case versus 4 for the person that finished it.  It also has math that encourages it to be brutal - the worst cards are 3 times worse than the best card.  Simply shifting the cards to be 2/3/4 instead of 1/2/3 lowers the variance significantly while still leaving it random enough for the desired effect.

RATING: 3

For example following things do not create a great game in my opinion: Lack of control, huge downtime, fair amount of random, lack of choices. These are all nicely combined in the Saboteur.

I wonder if the game would be better with smaller number of players, but it would require a very sharp stick to force me to play this game again and try.

The idea itself is ok, but game play is not. Secret roles with different victory conditions is a good thing, building the tunnels is nice, but the end result is bad.

RATING: 6

Not the best game but good as a filler with many people. Timing is a big aspect here, you shouldn't give away that you are the traitor to early but not to late, either.

RATING: 4.8

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 3.5
This is one of the few games that after few tries I would argue to be "flawed". Being ridiculously outnumbered, saboteurs have a close to impossible task to accomplish.
On the other hand there are simply too many map cards: in every game all players had their chances to check at at least one destination card, and being the saboteurs less than half (and usually less than a third, and since we played with 6 we had almost always only ONE saboteur!) lying on the destinations can spoil the traitor identity in no time.
Being strongly outnumbered, once a saboteur is located, he is basically out of the game, as every player can stack a blocking action card onto him. At this point only having a buddy with a handful of unblocking action can help, but only up to a certain point, since helping him would spoil his own identity as well. But wait, even if you have the cards to unlock yourself or your buddy this will take away your turn, and the other players will eventually be able to block you further or reach the treasure.

So in the end, being the saboteur brings you out of the winning league with about 90% of the chances. Saboteurs can really win only if they are very lucky with card distribution (many tunnel-collapse card in their hand for example).
The bluffing is there, but up to a certain point. A saboteur could ideally play a tunnel card that is not beneficial to reach the treasure with the reasoning that he couldn't play anything else, but (a) either there are no spots to play that card with less impact (otherwise his move would spoil his identity) or (b) that card doesn't interfere with the path to the treasure (and being the saboteurs quite few in number this action just delays the reaching of the treasure by one turn).

To summarize, the big letdown for me is that saboteurs are in exceptionally strong disadvantage. They have to keep their identity secret, because once they are revealed they can be thrown out of the game easily, but to keep their identity secret they have too few means to interfere with gnomes' plans.
In the end, all of our games ended up with a podium made of people who had been saboteurs the least.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
